text:
I'm giving this five stars for this recipe w/ modifications. I think you will really love this if you try it the way I did!

I seasoned the chops w/ s,p, and garlic powder, then dredged in flour seasoned w/ pepper, garlic powder, paprika, and some Emrils all-purpose seasoning....&
browned in olive oil.

On the stove, I boiled the water w/ one large chicken bouillon cube, then reduced, and added one can of cream of mushroom soup. I wisked together about 4 T flour in some cold water and added it to this saice. I let this simmer a little.
Poured over chops and onions in crock pot. Right before it is finished, or even after it is done, then add 8 oz. sour cream and stir around. 
This was tasty, creamy and great served over wide egg noodles and freshly steamed green beans sprinkled w/ lemon pepper.
Hope this review helps someone. I think the blandness some complained of will be alliviated w/ the extra seasonings in the flour mixture and the cr. of mushroom soup!! Try it!

Being that I saw this recipe at the last minute, I couldn't use my slow cooker, so I just browned my chops in my cast iron skillet with the onions, removed the chops just long enough to make a roux, added two cups of chicken broth instead of the water and simmered for forty five minutes. After they were done I again removed them from the skillet and added the sour cream and cooked for a minute. They came out so tender and the sauce was excellent! Good one Ami!!

text:
absolutly fabulous!  Bear with my changes, but I thought they might help someone else!  I used 5, two inch thick chops, seasoned with s,p,gp (salt, pepper, garlic powder), THEN I dreged them through highly seasoned flour (just use what you like).  I browned them in garlic infused oil.  I then browned the onions and put them on top of chops in crock pot.  For the sauce, I used 2 cups cx. broth, seasoned with fresh garlic, paprika, s,p,gp, and few other random things, and 1 can cream of mushroom soup.  Poured it over chops and cooked on LOW for 5 hours...could have just been 4 hours though.  Last, I added sauteed fresh mushrooms and the sour cream after moving chops to oven.  I think I should have used only 4 oz. sour cream though.  It was perfectly thick and very rich!  We loved it!

text:
This was a HUGE hit with my family.  I took heed of the reviews that claimed it was low on flavor and added a few changes.  My first change was that I coated the pork chops in roasted garlic and red pepper spice mix and THEN dredeged them in flour and browned them.  Then I cut the onions along with some quartered mushrooms and sliced a red pepper.  I carmelized all of these in a pan with a little olive oil.  YUM.  Then I followed the directions exactly except for the end where I noticed the sauce wasn't as thick as I would like.  I had no cream of mushroom soup so I threw in some cream cheese.  It was thick and flavorful and delicious!

text:
Maybe I shouldn't give this 5 stars, since I changed it so much, but my kids and hubby loved this recipe.  I didn't have time for the slow cooker so I did everything in a skillet on top of the stove.  I used chicken broth rather than bouillon cubes, and I left out the flour.  After simmering for a while, I took off the lid and the sauce thickened up nicely without flour (and since I'm on a low carb diet, it worked better for me).  I browned one chopped onion and a can of mushrooms along with the unbreaded breakfast-style boneless chops in the skillet, drained away what little olive oil I used, then mixed the broth and sour cream along with the spices I usually use for pork chops.  After simmering for about 25 minutes, I added a splash of balsamic vinegar just to deepen the flavors.  There wasn't a drop of this sauce left, or a scrap of meat.

text:
WOW! My husband and I LOVED these pork chops! I usually go by the recipe exactly the first time I make it but I had to make a couple changes to this one to save time. I did not coat the pork chops in flour and fry them in oil before putting them in the slow cooker, I simply coated them with salt, pepper, onion powder, and garlic powder and put them straight in the slow cooker. I followed the rest of the directions and when they were done cooking I did not put them in the oven on 200, that will only dry them out. I put them in a dish with a bit of the juice from the crock pot. Then I took all the juice/onions from the crock pot and put it in a small saucepan and added the flour/sour cream and cooked on medium heat while stirring, this was MUCH quicker than waiting for it to thicken up in the crock pot! I also added some extra seasoning to the sauce. They were delicious! I will be making this recipe on a regular basis!

I used McCormic Garlic Pepper to season the chops and fried them lightly without using flour. I cooked them on high in the crock-pot for 4 hours.(They were tender at this point but not falling apart.) I put the pork chops on a plate and then dumped all the liquid from the crock- pot into a sauce pan.  I added a packet of Mushroom gray mix and brought to a boil stirring continuously. After that I put the pork chops back in the crock-pot and poured the sauce over top and cooked on low for another 3 hours. MMMMMMMMMMM - Delicious!  The pork chops fell apart and mixed with the gravy.  I served it over mashed potatoes. My husband made an open-faced sandwhich.  Perfect comfort food for a cold night!

text:
This recipe is great as written!! Most of the time I skip the whole browning process though. I season the chops or pork steaks with salt, pepper, garlic powder, emerils or seasoning salt. I layer the onions starting with onions on the bottom and between the layers of chops. I use chicken broth from a box and pour in without heating. I start it out on high for two or three hours and finish it on low about 5 hours. I remove the chops and keep warm in oven while I prepare the sauce. I strain the broth into a sauce pan then add the sour cream and flour or corn starch and heat and stir until thickened. Comes out beautiful without lumps. I then pour some of the sauce over the chops and save the rest for rice or noodles. I love serving this with rice,  greens, blackeyed peas or beans and corn bread muffins. It is a great comfort food meal with a down home feel!! My whole family loves this!!

text:
These were super tasty and moist. I followed the ingredient list, but I did have to alter the cooking method. I browned the chops on the stove in some olive oil with the onions. I removed the onions and chops after browning so I could make a rue with 2 tbsp flour and 2 tbsp butter. I then added the pork chops back in with the onions. I then added the chicken bouillon / water mixture. I cooked on the stovetop on medium low for 45 minutes. After finished cooking I removed the chops and added the sour cream to the sauce. Not a single drop of the sauce or chops were left. Very good recipe.

These chops came out absolutely amazing!  It is now one of our favorite dishes.  I also made a few changes based on the other reviews.  I seasoned the pork chops with seasoning salt, dredged in flour and then browned them in a little olive oil and added fresh garlic.  I moved them to the crock pot and threw in chopped onioins, a can of cream of mushroom soup and a combination of chicken and beef broth (2 cups total; didn't have enough of one to do all the same). text:
This is a wonderful recipe! Good enough for a company dinner. I basically took some of the other suggestions and made them my own. One suggestion is to use boneless pork chops and then to cut all visible fat from them prior to cooking them. The chops become so tender that they do fall right off the bone. Then you are left with all these little bone fragments in the sauce along with the fat that has detached from the meat. Next time I will take care of that in advance by using boneless chops and cutting off fat first. I too seasoned chops. I used Santa Maria Style Seasoning which is just salt, pepper, garlic, and parsley. Then I dredged the chops in flour that I seasoned with salt, pepper, garlic and paprika. Lightly fried them on each side in a combo of olive oil/butter. Boiled my water and disolved the chicken cube and then added one can cream of mushroom soup to chicken broth. Heated and stirred until creamy. I sliced my onion and sauted it in the pan juices where I had fried the chops after I removed them to the crock pot. Then added the softened onions to the chicken/mushroom soup mixture and stirred until creamy. I then poured the chicken broth/mushroom soup/ onion mixture over the chops in the crock pot and cooked it on low for about 7 hours. They were probably done after about 5 hours. Served over rice. Delicious!

This was the advice I followed from another user!  I'm giving this five stars for this recipe w/ modifications. I think you will really love this if you try it the way I did! I seasoned the chops w/ s,p, and garlic powder, then dredged in flour seasoned w/ pepper, garlic powder, paprika, and some Emrils all-purpose seasoning....& browned in olive oil. On the stove, I boiled the water w/ one large chicken bouillon cube, then reduced, and added one can of cream of mushroom soup. I wisked together about 4 T flour in some cold water and added it to the sauce.  I added it all to the slow cooker with half an onion diced into small pieces.  I also added a can of drained mushrooms.  My family LOVED this one!!

text:
Delicious!  And a great way to fix pork chops without thoroughly frying them on stovetop.   I used 8 boneless butterfly chops, slow-cooked them on High for 4 hours, though I think next time, I'll see if they're done at 3 hours.  They were falling-apart tender, but just a wee bit on the dry side, but the gravy was outstanding, and had lots of if (we like a lot of gravy).  I used 2 cups of chicken broth for the bouillon and water, and 3 tbsp flour.  If you like it a bit more tangy, double the sour cream.  We served it with mashed potatoes (put some of the gravy on) and green beans.  There was so much gravy left over after the chops were eaten, my boyfriend sopped it up with some bread and finished it off!  Thanks for a good recipe.

Like other reviewers, I added cream of mushroom soup.  I also threw in some mushrooms, as we love them.  I only had about six hours, so I cooked on high for two and then low for four.  My chops were so tender they broke apart.  I mixed half the sauce into rice, put the chops on top, and covered them with more sauce. UPDATE:  Since the first time I've made this, I realize that the mushroom soup is completely useless.  The sour cream makes a perfectly creamy sauce all on it's own. This is an A+ recipe and works every time!

text:
This was actually very good.  Not too many changes since I prefer to follow the directions as given.  I do like to read other reviews first and then make changes that I think would be beneficial to avoid wasting time (i.e., bland, too watery, etc.).  I  seasoned the flour with a pretty good amount of salt, pepper and garlic powder.  Dredged boneless pork chops (with fat on) in the seasoned flour and cooked in skillet with a little olive oil/butter mix, until lightly browned.  Mixed 1 c. beef broth and 1 c. chicken broth (I think beef broth adds a little more flavor), together with 1/2 to 3/4 can of cream of mushroom soup and added to slow cooker and stirred until smooth.  Add pork  chops.  Then, rather than just add the sliced onions I put them in the same skillet I used to brown the chops and cooked a few minutes until softened (add a tbsp. of broth to loosen any bits of pork still on the bottom of pan).  Add them to the slow cooker, stir, and cook on low for 7-8 hrs.  When finished, I placed the pork chops on a dish and kept warm in the oven.  I then placed the juice from the slow cooker, including onions, into a sauce pan, added approx. 4 oz. sour cream and approx. 2 tbsp. flour and heated until thickened to my liking.   Served with extra wide egg noodles.  Everyone agreed it was very flavorful without being a heavy dish. You can always add additional salt, pepper or garlic powder if needed.  Rather than using the full amount of sour cream, I chose to use half the sour cre

So good! it's just me and my husband so i halved the recipe--three bone-in pork chops plus the recipe as written essentially. I dredged the pork chops with s&p, flour, dried thyme and garlic powder, browned them and cooked for 4 hours on high with an onion and chicken broth (instead of bouillon). I did sub plain Greek yoghurt as we were out of sour cream and added s&p plus some thyme and garlic powder as an earlier taste test seemed a bit bland. Amazing. We will make again, esp. with mashed potatoes to go with the yummy sauce.

Made this yesterday for my family. Based on many reviews I added the can of cream of mushroom soup; otherwise I made no changes. The dish was delicious: creamy but not too rich, filling, and very, very easy. Served it over wide egg noodles. Filled the slow cooker with the browned chops on a Saturday night and set it to simmer on low before leaving for church. This is comfort food at its best,  mainly because everyone loved it and it was soooooo easy to make.

The Pork chops themselves rate 10 stars! Used 6 thick boneless chops, seasoned with garlic salt and lots of pepper, floured and fried till nice and brown. Followed instructions, except added 3 large gloves of chopped minced garlic, from my garden springs of Rosemary, Thyme and Sage. Removed the fresh herb sprigs and leaves, and the chops as directed, tasted juices and it was very flavorful, but felt it needed some richness so I added one beef bouillon and it was perfect! text:
I too used mushroom soup, but used Golden Mushroom Soup mixed with about 3/4 can of skim milk and 1/2 cup cream cheese. I sauteed a sliced onion and a small package of Baby Bella mushrooms, put them in the pot first. Seasoned 4 2-inch pork chops with McCormicks Montreal Steak Seasoning and browned them. Added them to the pot, then the sauce over all. After 4 hours (half on high, half on med.) the chops were perfect, but the sauce was too thin, so I scooped most of into a sauce pan and boiled it for 30 minutes with 2 T. flour/water mixture.  That thickened it up nicely, so then I added 1/2 cup of sour cream and back into the pot with the chops.  It was very very tasty, and there is enough sauce left with the 2 extra chops to serve again with noodles or smashed potatoes. Great recipe.

text:
Great recipe! You can make this in less than 15 min by using pork cutlets and 1 pan on the stovetop.  Use a plastic bag to combine flour and seasonings, and then shake to coat pork chops.  Brown in pan with cooking spray and a little butter/margarine.  Once browned on both sides, add broth (I used chicken b/c its what I had on hand) and let simmer.  I added mushrooms here too (if using onions, do before). Then pull off heat once chops are cooked and stir in sour cream.  Serve!  PS-save flour from bag and use it to thicken your broth before you stir in sour cream.  Goes grat with crusty bread, rice, or noodles for extra sauce.

city:

country:

text:
While I ended up with a good result, I think the recipe needs tweaking. I recognize that 'flavor' is subjective and as written this wouldn't have enough for us. I seasoned the flour that I dredged the pork in as well as seasoning the chops themselves. I think the browning step is important because it seals flavor into the meat before adding any liquid to it.  I sliced and added an 8 oz package of crimini mushrooms after an hour of cooking which also added flavor to the sauce as they cooked down. I think the timing in the instructions is way off and would end up overcooking the meat.  I cooked the chops for 4 hours on low. They were tender but still held their shape and were not dry at all. I also think the advice of putting them in the oven is not wise and would result in some drying out. Instead, I piled these on a plate and covered them tightly with foil while thickening the sauce. I chose this recipe specifically because it did NOT call for Cream of Anything soup so I followed the instructions for this part. While my sauce did thicken up, I do understand why you would choose the stove top route if you were in a hurry. I wasn't, so after thickening the sauce I ended up adding a bit more sour cream and a good solid helping of dill weed to give it more flavor. I nestled the chops back in the sauce and left the crock pot on warm for another hour until serving. The sour cream and dill flavor really worked for us - a little reminiscent of a stroganoff.

This is similar to a baked Sour Cream Chicken recipe I've used for years. For those who found this pork chop recipe bland, here is the chicken recipe which has a few more flavor ideas you might try: 1 1/2c plain yogurt or sour cream, 1/4 c lemon juice, 1/2 tsp paprika, 1 garlic clove, 1/2 tsp Worcestershire sauce, 1/2 tsp salt, 1/4 tsp pepper; marinate overnight, coat with bread crumbs and bake at 350 for 45 min.

text:
Yum! I probably shouldn't rate this since I did a few things differently. I pulled what I thought was a small roast out of the freezer and after defrosting I found that it was 3 meaty pork steaks. It was a little late to use the slow cooker so I shook my steaks in a plastic bag with flour and the seasonings. I browned them and the onion in my cast iron skillet and seasoned them again with a garlic herb seasoning. I then added two cans of chicken broth and simmered it for about 45 minutes or so. I removed the meat and I shook in a little of the superfine, quick mixing flour and whisked it along with the sour cream and then put the meat back in. The gravy was excellent! I served it with mashed potatoes and steamed broccoli. With pork steaks being so fatty, it was so tender and along with the sour cream it wasn't exactly lo-cal but it was delicious and 
so quick and easy. Thank you AMI.

text:
A keeper - will definitely make again!  As a previous reviewer, I only found this recipe a few hours before it was time to cook the chops so no time to use slow cooker.  Following instructions for flouring and browning, then added approx 1 cup of chicken stock (for 4 chops) with a good sprinkling of onion flakes (neither my husband nor I can eat 'real' onion anymore).  Simmered, covered, for 45 minutes on stove, removed the chops to a warm oven and added about 1/2 fat free sour cream and 1 tbsp flour mixed with a little sour cream to the pan.  They turned out wonderfully!  Served the sauce over the chops and potatoes and have enough for another meal.  Much prefer this sauce to ones based on "cream of ..." soups.  Thanks so much for sharing.

Like some of the other reviewers, I was forced to try this recipe in the oven, due to lack of time.  My chops were thick cut, and 30 minutes at 400 degrees didn't give me the "falling apart" result I was hoping for.  Next time, I'll plan ahead for the slow cooker, or maybe an hour in the oven at 325.  As for taste...EXCELLENT!!! I will definitely make this one of my stand-by recipes!

text:
Fantastic! Im not really a pork chop fan bec it always turns out dry. This was my first time making it in the slow-cooker and it was soo tender. The first step I kept the same (except added basil). 2nd I sauted the onion than added the water and cube. Put broth in pot and on low for 4 hours. I took about a cup of broth out of cooker mixed cream of mush,sour cream,mushrooms, squeezed half a lemon and seasoned. Than put on top of chops. I had with mashed potatoes and carrots. I really liked this and am going to make again. I will always do my chops in the slow cooker from now on.:::UPDATE::: Made this again bec I liked it soo much! There was a sale on Pork Chops. I didnt think they differ too much. I bought Sirlion Pork Chops and made this again exactly as stated and It turned out really dry!! Will def never buy Sirlion Chops again:( Im going to stick with bone-in regular Chops!!

My family enjoyed this recipe.  I did not feel that the sauce was bland.  I used fat-free sour cream and the sauce had a tangy light sour cream flavor which was enough for me.  I do not want a sauce that overpowers just compliments.  I did make sure to generously season the pork chops before dredging in the flour.  I did not feel like using my slowcooker so I baked them according to another pork chop recipe I have.  I used 1 can chicken broth instead of the bouillon and baked them for 45 minutes in a 350 oven.  After removing the chops from the broth, I sprinkled some mozzarella cheese on top.  Served noodles and cauliflower on the side.  I spooned some of the sauce over the noodles and since the meal was very white I sprinkled some chives over the noodles.  I really enjoyed this and my husband went back for seconds so I will definitely make this again.  My 2 boys 5 and 3 ate without complaint.

Obviously didn't use the slow cooker, just a cast iron pot, browned them in olive oil and butter, deglazed the pot with a little red wine, more butter, added the water, can of mushroom soup, onion, dumped the chops back in, and simmered while the rest of my meal cooked. text:
This was super awesome!  I hate crock pot recipes that make me cook before I put things in the crock, so I skipped the browning step like another reviewer did.  Just threw my 6 frozen pork chops in the crock and put in some seasonings on top. I used a LOT of garlic salt, some pepper, and sprinkled in a little flour (although I doubt that made any difference).  Followed all the other directions.  The pork chops were very tender after 8 hours (shocker).  I didn't have a lot of time to waste thickening a sauce in the crock pot, so after I removed the chops, I just poured the broth into a saucepan to thicken with the sour cream and flour.  Served over rice, it was a perfect homey meal that my whole family (including my 19 month old) chowed down.  Next time, the only change I make will be to cook maybe 2 - 3 more chops.  I had lots of extra sauce and no chops to put them on.  There was more than enough broth for a couple more chops.

My dh and I really enjoyed these pork chops.  Per other reviews, I used seasoning salt for the salt, added 1/2 teas. text:
I fixed this for dinner last night.  When trying a new recipe I always ask "Should I make this again?". This was squarely in the "Make Again" category.  I basically followed the instructions.  I was very liberal in the use of garlic powder and used Mrs. Dash's poultry seasoning instead of salt.  I figure there was more than enough salt coming from the boullion cubes. I cooked the pork chops for about 6 hrs on low and they were fall-apart tender.  I also ended up transfering the "gravy" mixture to a pot on the stove so it would thinking faster.  I served it with boiled new potatoes and mixed veggies. It is great to find a recipe for the crockpot that doesn't rely on "cream of something" soup.

Saw this as the featured recipe today and decided to give it a try.  I followed the recipe as listed with the following exceptions, I used 2 cups of chicken broth instead of cubes, I added extra onions bc we LOVE them, and I placed a few medium sized potatoes in the microwave for 3 minutes and then placed them on top to cook with the meat so I didn't have to make another side dish. It is a very good "throw in the crock" and let it cook itself meal that we will try again.  Next time I will season the meat a bit more bc we thought it was missing a little something.

all i can say is wow!  this was incredible.  i mixed in a tablespoon of garlic salt and a tablespoon of paprika to my flour mixture.  as many other reviewers, i didn't realize this was a crockpot recipe until it was too late.  i seared them in the pan and then baked in oven at 400 for 30min exactly as you would make for the crock pot.  i then took the juices, added about 1/4c of flour that was left from dredging (with spices mixed in) and used that to thicken the juices on the stove.  this made plenty of sauce to serve over the chops and egg noodles.  my family devoured this... it was incredibly flavourful.

I, like another reviewer (Linda McLean), didn't make this in the slow cooker, just on the stove top. I followed her instructions - browned the chops, made a roux, simmered in broth and then added the sour cream.  I also cooked some mushrooms and a bit of bacon in butter and then threw those in with the sour cream.  Heavenly!  The chops were SO tender and the sauce excellent! I love recipes that give you completely different results with almost the same ingredients!  I will be making this often, both ways!

text:
We just finished dinner. Nobody here liked this. The gravy never thickened, and it was terribly bland. I used the 2 tbsp flour AND added 4 tbsp additional cornstarch, and it still didn't thicken.   
The recipe didn't specify whether to use boneless or bone-in pork chops.  I used 6 boneless, and there was 10 times the amount of gravy than we needed for the amount of porkchops.  It also didn't tell you whether to replace the lid on the crockpot after adding the sour cream.  Putting the lid on created condensation and made it watery; keeping the lid off didn't allow the crockpot to get hot enough to thicken the gravy.  
This was a waste of good pork chops.

I did although use an alternative cooking method, Clay roaster w/ lid in a 325 oven for 2.5 hours with 7 bone in chops, amazing*****i just floured, browned in olive oil layered in my clay roaster, layered sliced onion in between chops and on top and poured the chicken broth in , covered and when done, all in, about 2.5 hours, I could not believe the finished result! Have made this per listed recipe and my own take. Both are excellent.  I do prefer my recipe, although it is per each person's taste.  I rate original 4 stars, mine 5.  If monies prevail, please get yourselves a Ninja cooker, it has a stove top and slow. You can brown and then slow cook, same pot. EASY-PEASY. Far less dishes and cleanup is the bomb with a Ninja, you could simply wipe with a paper towel. I have served over noodles and rice, delish both ways. I don't use soups, don't need, have added mushrooms.  I don't use flour after browning, I use a small amount of corn starch mix with water or chicken broth, and WALLA, instant thick. which at that time you switch back to stove cook.  SO so yummy, tender, not dry at all.  Enjoy folks.

Delicious!  SO impressed with the sauce.  I made this on the stove top as others did, and only used one chicken bouillon and omitted the flour in the sour cream as it didn't need it. text:
This was one of the best dishes I have ever made and I am not a great cook. It was absolutely delicious. I am from Oklahoma, and it really did come out like good old fashioned smothered pork chops. My boyfriend gave me highest marks, saying "these pork chops are on hit!" (that's a good thing) No changes are necessary with this recipe, but I did lower the servings to 4 chops,caramelized the onions in the skillet before adding to the crock pot (although I don't know if that was even necessary since the onions almost completely emulsified during cooking), and used vegetable bouillon vs beef bc that's all I had.Here is a big change I made, I cooked on high for 5 1/2 hours vs on low for 8 to 9 hrs bc I simply didn't have time. Still came out super tender, no knife was necessary! I also poured the crock pot droppings in a sauce pan and made the gravy over the stove with the sour cream and flour, vs in the crock pot - as 1 reviewer said, saves TONS of time, your gravy will be ready in like 4 mins. It was perfectly thick, I did strain it to get the flour lumps out. Use tons of seasoning before browning,it will have great flavor. I also used lean chops which worked well with this dish. I served it with a wild rice and broccoli mix I got from one of those Knorr heat-up "rice sides" bags and a salad. Love the fact that ingredients were simple and all on hand. The only complaint is you end up with tons of dirty pots and pans, which is not normal for a crock pot recipe. But still 5 stars!

These were excellent. I basically followed the recipe, adding more spices to fit my tastes, including a quarter packet of onion soup. I seasoned the chops, seasoned some flour, dredged em, browned them in olive oil, and transferred to crock pot. I mixed the 2 cups water and bullion cubes to the pan I cooked the chops in to keep all that yummy goodness. I also pulled the chops out at the end (they really do fall apart) and transferred the liquid and onions into a pan, added the sour cream and flour mixture, and stirred til it thickened.

My man doesn't care much for chops and he went back for thirds on these.

This was so easy, and so good! I used garlic salt instead of garlic powder for a little extra kick. text:
We LOVED this recipe, but I did modify to "our" preferences.  I'm sure it would be great as is but we just like more spice/gravy.

I doubled the recipe as I always do for my "big" eating family!   I browned the prepared and heavily seasoned pork chops and set aside.  I sauted 4 cloves of fresh garlic with the onion, then poured 1 can of cream of mushroom soup in the same pan mixing in with the brown particles from the pork..YUM.  I then added boiling water/bouillon (probably a bit more than written) and slowly added a mixture of corn starch and water to the mix.  Placed the pork chops on the bottom of my large crock pot and then poured the "gravy" mix over the chops.  Cooked approximately 5 hours on low setting and carefully removed chops to a platter.   Added sauted "fresh" mushrooms (approx. 16 oz.) and container of sour cream.  Mixed gravy well, then put chops back in to the crock pot and continued to cook maybe an hour longer.  The chops were already done, but we were not ready to eat yet.  The house SMELLED AMAZING!!!!  Served over Polish egg noodles with seasoned fresh green beans.  It is not a pretty dish, but the TASTE IS AMAZING!!!!  My family from ages 8 to 55 LOVED this dish.  I WILL DEFINITELY BE MAKING THIS AGAIN AND AGAIN!!!!  SOOOOO GOOD!  I used center cut pork chops "with" bone so had to be careful as some small bones were left in sauce.  But that little tid bit didn't bother my family at all.  SMELLS & TASTE AMAZING........sooooo TENDER you will LOVE!

text:
Would give this more than 5 stars if I could! I had to make a couple of modifications because of time and ingredients.  My chops were still frozen and I was running late, so I skipped browning them first - just put them straight into the crockpot and seasoned with the salt, pepper and garlic powder.  I used 2 cups chicken broth instead of bouillon and water.  Didn't have 7-8 hours to allow them to cook so I cooked them on high for about 5 hours.  Instead of turning on the oven, I removed the chops to a plate, poured the liquid into a sauce pan and then put the chops back into the crock pot to stay warm.  I allowed the sauce to cook on top of the stove for about 15 minutes and it thickened nicely.  The pork chops were fork tender and the onions added great flavor.  I served the chops on brown rice and poured the sauce over the top.  Absolutely delicious and I will definitely be making them again - this recipe is perfect as written and doesn't need any ingredient changes.  I don't understand why people drastically modify recipe ingredients and then rate it - just submit your own recipe.

text:
Although this dish didn't "wow" me, it was very tasty and I can't think of any complaints about it or changes I'd make.  I don't have a slow cooker, and I was only cooking one chop for myself, so I put the pork chop into a small pyrex bowl with the broth after seasoning the pork chop w/ salt, pepper & garlic powder.  I added sliced mushrooms on top.  I cooked in the oven covered for 55 minutes at 375 degrees.  When I took it out of the oven, I poured the broth in a saucepan with the sour cream and very little cornstarch and heated through.  I poured this over my pork chop.  Very tasty, very easy, and one of the most tender chops I've had!

A decent "base" recipe, but it would've been quite bland. I added smoked Paprika to the flour mixture and also sprinkled it directly on the meat before I browned it (I used a Pork Shoulder roast) . To the sauce, I added 2 tsp's Worst. sauce and a can of Cream Mush. Soup. When it came time to add the sour cream, I added a tablspoon of cornstarch to the s.c. and while that was in the crock pot, I sliced up the meat, added it back to the sauce and then served over Egg Noodles.  It turned out a lot like a stroganoff.

text:
Made these tonight and they turned out moist and tender.  I incorporated feedback from others and changed 2 cups. water to 1 cup water, and added 1 cup chix. stock.  I didn't cook in slow cooker because of time, but I did season & flour chops before I browned them in pan with oil, transferred to baking dish, then I put onions in pan to saute', added some sliced mushrooms.  Mixed up sour cream with remaining flour mixture, added water/chix stock and bouillon.  I did taste this and was not pleased, tasted like watered down flour paste, so I added seasonings (salt, pepper, garlic powder a little white wine, worcestershire) and flavor improved.  Poured this over chops, added onions & mushrooms, put in 350 oven for 1 hour, reduced temp. to 200 for another hour and they tasted great.  I also baked potatoes at the same time.  I'm planning on this for a special dinner tomorrow and can't wait to top my potato with some of the sauce.  I will make these again.

OMG i loved this receipe,i just changed a few things. First i used a pork roast instead of pork chops, (you get more meat for your buck and no bones to deal with)  I used 1 bouillon cube with 1cup of water and 1 can of chicken stock.  Then I sauteed my onions in the grease left over from browning the roast, i added about 1/4 c of chicken stock to the onions and let it cook out then poured over the meat and cooked it all day..mmmmm

Instant classic at our house. Only change I made was spicing up the flour with some white pepper and paprika.  My chops were on the thin side so 4.5 hours in the crockpot on low was plenty. Sauce could have been a bit thicker.  Next time I will either remove some of the broth before adding the flour and sour cream or maybe use more flour. Served this with Peppridge Farm Stuffing and asparagus.  Dinner hit the table 30 minutes after I hit the door.  YAY!!!

text:
This recipe has a lot of potential. I did all the prep work in the morning and the pork browned up beautifully.  However, I was gone for about nine hours which was WAY too long to have these in the slow cooker so by the time I got home the meat was overcooked and there was hardly any liquid left so I had to add a can of crm mushroom soup and some milk. Moral of the story- the pork only needs to cook for about 4-5 hours. Otherwise, the taste was great!

text:
I was looking for a new and easy pork chop recipe and decided to try this one. I made a few changes. I added garlic powder, salt, pepper, and onion powder to my flour before browning in 1 tsp of olive oil.

I also used one can of cream of mushroom soup and one can golden mushroom soup. I mixed them together in a bowl with fresh minced garlic, fresh mushrooms, 1 1/2 cans of milk, dash of garlic salt, and pepper. 

I cooked them on low for 9 hours. The one thing that bothered me was that the gravy or soup mix really stuck to the sides of the crock pot and browned pretty bad. 

The pork chops were very moist they were falling off the bone Next time will use boneless chops. I added 3 tbsp of sour cream to the gravy mix about an hour before serving and it seemd to thicken it up quite a bit.

My husband loved these! The meat was very tender. I found it to be a bit dry, but falvorful. I served this with egg noodles, green beans and a salad.

Next time I think I will cook for a shorter period of time maybe for 6 hours.

Overall great and easy recipe. I love being able to put something together in the morning and being able to walk away from it until later!

Thanks for an easy recipe...my family loved it!

text:
Very good recipe!!  Along with a previous reviewer...I got this recipe late in the day today....too late for the crock pot.  SO...I peppered and floured the pork chops (skipped the salt) browned them...then added a can of beef broth, the chopped onions and a packet of beefy onion soup...covered and let simmer for 45 minutes.  Then I took out the pork chops...stirred in the sour cream and it came out fantastic!  I may try low sodium beef broth next time as the gravy was a little salty...but all in all it was perfect!!!  I made mashed potatoes on the side...my picky husband and 4 year old daughter gobbled it up!!  Thanks!

text:
These pork chops were fantastic!  Very moist and tender!  After removing the browned chops from the skillet, I melted about 2 tablespoons of butter in the pan, added the sliced onions, sprinkled with a little salt, and sauteed them for about 3 - 4 minutes, stirring constantly.  This helped to release the flavor of the onions before adding them to the pork chops in the slow cooker.  I also used low sodium chicken broth instead of bouillon and water.  The chops were perfectly done in about 4 and a half hours. Served with mashed potatoes and the yummy sour cream gravy, my husband said they were the best chops he had ever eaten!

Love it!  My changes:  seasoned with a ton of cracked pepper on both sides before searing on high.  Then pretty much follow the rest exactly as written.  I have made in the oven as well, low heat like 200/250, and cook for 3-4 hours which is fine.  Also, I use thick cut, bone in pork chops for best results.  But, cooking low and slow yields a tender, fall apart chop even if not using a bone-in cut.  I have also made it with mushrooms, and if I didn't have chicken stock or broth, I have used beef or store bought pork.

text:
I made this almost to the recipe but since I don't like garlic and onions I omitted those and added some general poultry seasoning along with the salt, pepper, paprika to the flour before dredging the chops.  Everything else was to the letter.  I browned the chops in some oil before putting in the crockpot but I might try skipping this step next time to see if makes much of a difference because it would make it easier to make before running off to work in the morning.  I've never had pork chops so tender before in my life!  I didn't need to use a knife once even after reheating the leftovers the next day in the microwave for lunch!  Served with broccolini and  mashed potatoes.  This makes a lot of sauce (about 2 cups) so we had extra even after adding to the mashed potatoes.  We kept it to use on something else we cook this week because it was good and don't want to waste it!

This was good. I really liked the process of things, especially the sour cream sauce. My only complaint is, while I loved that the meat was fall off the bone tender, I did not like that the bones fell apart. It was very hard to distinguish between bone and meat just by looking at it...and no matter how careful my husband and I were, we both managed to get a mouthful of smaller bones at least once. Perhaps boneless pork chops would be better but it may compromise the flavor. If I make these again I will keep a better eye on the cooking time. I only cooked for 5.5 hours on low this time. I guess my crock pot cooks faster than average. Flavor was nice though and we ate this over egg noodles with a side of roasted Brussel sprouts.

text:
Although our pork chops came out wonderfully, I am only giving this recipe 4 stars because I deviated so far away from it, but owe my inspiration to the original recipe! Seasoned the chops with S/P, Paprika and  garlic, then seared them on the stove top. placed the onion, chops, and more garlic in Slow Cooker, then covered with Progresso Cream of Mushroom Soup (I am Gluten intolerant and Progresso is the only creamy soup I can find without added flour). Later added about a cup of wine and several drained cans of sliced mushrooms. I have a tendency to sniff herbs combined with the scent of the cooker to evaluate what goes with what , so I added several herbs that seemed to enhance the flavor (can't remember which herbs, but my method does work!) It really made the house smell heavenly. My hubby said it reminded him of "Pork Stroganoff". 4 hours was all that was needed to provide succulent chops that still held together.

Delicious! I butterflied large boneless center cut chops. seasoned with a garlic powder and a light breadcrumb mix rather than flour. Baked for about 15 min at 350. text:
This was really good but I worked with what I had. 4 - 1 1/2 inch boneless chops. I spiced them and fried them in garlic and white truffle oil enough to brown slightly. Dredged in flower,  placed in crock pot. Fried 1/2 onion and 2 cups leeks in leftover oil. Added 1/2 a can of chicken broth to bottom of crock pot and the rest to the frying pan. After leeks/onion cooked down I added them on top of chops. Cooked on low 4 hours. Last half hour I sprinkled 2 Tlb flower over chops added 1/2 can cream of chicken soup a cup of sour cream. Cooked 1/2 hour. Served over white rice. Yum. Moist and tender creamy.

This turned out to to be a good recipe. After reading the reviews I made a few changes. I mixed chicken stock, sour cream and a can of cream of celery together. With the pork chops, I did a egg wash and coated with seasoned flour (garlic powder, onion powder, salt and pepper) and fried in olive oil.  I lined the bottom of the  slow cooker with onions. Before dinner was over everyone said this was a keeper.

Cooked the pasta & put it into the slow cooker too at the end. An all in one pot meal. I will definitely be making this again.

text:
As per reviewer; seasoned the chops w/ s,p, & garlic and onion  powder, then dredged in flour seasoned w/ pepper, garlic powder, onion powder, paprika, and a little cayenne pepper... then browned in a little olive oil.  **OR ---I used 5, 2" thick chops, seasoned with s,p,gp (salt, pepper, garlic powder), THEN I dreged them through highly seasoned flour (just use what you like). I browned them in garlic infused oil. I then browned the onions & put them on top of chops in crock pot. For the sauce, I used 2 cups chicken broth, seasoned w/fresh garlic, paprika, s,p,gp, and few other random things, and 1 can cream of mushroom soup. Poured it over chops & cooked on LOW for 4 hours.  Last, I added sauteed fresh mushrooms & the sour cream AFTER moving chops to oven.  used only 4 oz. sour cream though..  per another reviewer;  I just browned my chops in my cast iron skillet w/onions, removed the chops just long enough to make a roux, added 2 cups of chicken broth instead of the water & simmered for 45  minutes. After they were done I again removed them from the skillet & added the sour cream & cooked for a minute.

text:
I did improvise a little on this recipe, but the foundation of it seemed like a good place to start. I used bone in pork chops. Seasoned my flour generously with seasoned salt, garlic, pepper, some chili powder. Browned the chops in a cast iron, took them out of the skillet, turned down the heat; added butter and then the onions. Turned up the heat; Sauted the onions until very brown and "smothered" and added them to the chops in the crock pot. I heated up some chicken broth, added a little flour/milk mix and stirred. Added most of this mixture to the crock pot. At the end I added fresh thyme and rosemary to the crock pot then the sour cream mixed with a little of the leftover broth. I made roasted cauliflower and garlic; mashed it up with butter and served it as a low carb side with the chops. It was delicious!!

text:
Since it was too late to make this in the slow cooker, I cooked these in my electric skillet & made the following modifications:
3 bone-in pork chops, approx. 1" thick
2 large onions, sliced
1 14.5oz. can low sodium chicken broth instead of bouillon cubes
1 10  oz. can cream of mushroom soup
1 small container of sour cream

I browned the chops until very dark in olive oil, sprinkling Lawry's Seasoned Salt, garlic powder & a little paprika on one side, Lawry's Seasoned Pepper & Herbes de Provence (a mixture of rosemary, thyme, basil, marjoram, fennel, sage, & lavender) on the other side while browning; removed chops & 
browned the onions in the same skillet.  Then I added enough flour to make a roux. When the roux had browned sufficiently, I added the mshrm. soup & chicken broth, which I had previously whisked together.  I then put the chops & onions back into the skillet with the liquids & cooked at the lowest heat to keep them cooking until the chops were falling apart. I removed the chops & stirred in the sour cream, heating until hot again.   I served it over rice.  It was absolutely delicious!  My husband said they were the best  chops he has ever eaten in his life (he's 73!) & the 'gravy' was brown & rich.  I will be making this very often.

text:
I didn't have time to make this is the crockpot, so I covered the porkchops in garlic, salt, and pepper and dredged in flour. Heated in olive oil until browned. Took them out and put them aside. Added a bit of white wine to get up the brown bits and cooked the onions until softened. Added the chicken broth and porkchops and simmered for about 20 min (I used thin porkchops). Took them out and added about 2 tsp flour and sour cream to the sauce and heated for about 5 minutes and topped the chops. Paired it with asparagus. Was very good.

text:
I made this for dinner tonight.  I cooked the chops for 7 hours on low in the crockpot as directed.  I then removed the chops and put them in a low heat oven.  I was a bit skeptical about putting only 2 T. of flour with the sour cream in the remaining liquid as there was so much liquid left.  Anyway, I did as directed with the sour cream and the flour and cooked on high in the crockpot for 30 minutes.  It didn't thicken as I wanted it to so I transferred it to a pot, put it on my gas stove and added about 3T of additional flour to thicken the gravy more.  This did the trick!  Overall, we loved it.  I will definitely make it again.

text:
Very moist tender chops - and I usually can't eat pork chops because of the texture.  I used rotisserie chicken seasoning before dredging the chops, sauteed the onion with garlic in olive oil, and then cooked them for 3 hours on high, 1 hour on low.  Popped them in a 200 degree oven while finishing up the sauce, and they were cooked perfectly.  The sauce really didn't thicken up much, and if I'd had the time, I probably would've added even more flour and cooked it on the stovetop - but it was good anyway.

Update - 1/9/14 - Made these tonight with the changes from the 'most helpful review', and I think it was even better.  Still used the rotisserie chicken seasoning, then threw the chicken broth in the pan to deglaze the pan and scrape up the browned bits.  I mixed in a can of cream of mushroom soup before adding it to the crockpot over the chops.  I sauted the onion in a little olive oil and added the garlic for a moment at the end, and then added just a bit more chicken broth.  Probably should've added the onions to the crockpot before the broth/soup mix, but it still worked out just fine.  I cooked about an hour on high and 4 hours on low, then removed chops to the oven to keep warm while thickening the sauce.  It made a LOT of sauce - no need to double.

text:
Oh my.... I've been eyeing this recipe some time now, and FINALLY decided to give it a try! My fiance can be "picky" sometimes, but usually eats whatever I put in front of him (even if he thinks it's gonna be icky). Tonight was the exception. My fiance ate one pork chop (he will ALWAYS try anything I put in front of him, even the strawberries he's hated since childhood lol) - that's it! It was the gravy that turned him off.... Since I covered our mashed potatoes with it, he wouldn't even eat those!!! I didn't find the gravy "repulsive," but wasn't jumping out of my seat to have seconds either. I pretty much followed Ami's directions exactly, except for subbing seasoned salt for plain table salt and adding all of my spices (i.e. seasoned salt, pepper, garlic powder) to my flour to save a step. Dredging my pork chops in a plastic Zip-lock bag made clean-up a breeze. Note: I had to pour my cooked liquid  / sour cream mixture (I mixed my sour cream and flour together before adding) into a saucepan and bring to a boil for several minutes to thicken. My gravy was still thinner than I liked.... I tried the slow cooker method suggested, but my sour cream wouldn't completely melt (looked gross). Oh well! My fiance would give this 0 stars, but to be fair (I thought this was "OK"), I'll give 3. Served with taters, green beans and dinner rolls, this was a filling meal. Thanks for sharing, AMI! :-)

text:
5 stars coming from a family who do not particularly like pork chops.  Finally a recipe where they don't come out dry AND have flavor. Followed ingrediant list and WAS going to put in slow cooker but a last minute realized my chops were very thin which meant the time would have been cut in half and I wouldn't be home to shut slow cooker or they would have definitely been dried out. So I put them in a ziploc after I seasoned and dredged in flour (added x garlic).  I used the skillet and followed all ingrediant list.  I added the sour cream the last 20-25 minutes.  They simmereed about an hour total.  Served w/rice and a salad.  They EASILY cut with a fork just so moist and flavorful.  Thank you for sharing.

text:
One it's own I think this recipe is 3 or maybe 4 stars. With some changes I think it can be 5. Most importantly I think the cook time should be adjusted. I had my chops on low for just under 7 hours, and while the meat did fall apart easily it was a little dry. Secondly is the sauce seasoning. I added about a half packet of onion soup mix and 3 chopped cloves of garlic. At the end when I added the sour cream & flour and turned it up to high it just didn't get hot enough for the sour cream to melt & the sauce to thicken, so I put it in a saucepot on the stove which made a beautiful sauce..and it was very yummy. I will make this again but will reduce the cook time to 4-5 hours on low, and will definitely add the onion soup mix.

text:
I gave this 4 stars because it is a "good bones" recipe...it needs more seasoning based on ones personal preferences but it supplies a good starting point.  
As other reviewers have noted, the sauce is a bit bland as written, but it is easily tweaked to suit your tastes.

I personally seasoned my chops with salt, pepper, and garlic when browning. I also added a wad of fresh tarragon to the sauce when I stirred in the sour cream.

Any fresh herb will make this a very tasteful dish as well as 'pretty'.

The sauce needed to be a bit thicker for my taste, so I added more flour to the sour cream.
